# To search for specific strin within a file, we will use grep command. We have to use the right path and uncopmress fastq.gs. Then, start using the searching command grep as it shown below:

# For redirection, we used the command below to redirct and put all the sequences that contains NNNNNN from all the files in to another file named bad_reads.txt.
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ grep -B1 -A2 NNNNNN NGS0001.R1.fastq > bad_reads.txt
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ ls -l

# The same step used for the next read (uncompressing and searching the sequence):
# The use of >> will append to rather than overwrite a file. This can be useful for saving more than one search as shown below:
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ zcat NGS0001.R2.fastq.gz > NGS0001.R2.fastq
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ grep -B1 -A2 NNNNNN NGS0001.R2.fastq >> bad_reads.txt
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ ls -l

# These commands used to create a new folder called other, and the bad_reads.txt moved to this other folder using the command mv.
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ mkdir ../other/
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ mv bad_reads.txt ../other/

# The pipe command (|) is a redirection command.
# We can pipe the grep command to less
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ grep -B1 -A2 NNNNNN NGS0001.R1.fastq | less

# The following command used to count the number of words (wc).
# It counts the number of lines or characters. So, we can use it to count the number of lines we're getting back from our grep command. 
# It will tell us how many sequences we're finding.
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ (base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ grep NNNNNN NGS0001.R1.fastq | wc
    555     555   56055

# Here, we don't need the command (wc) tells us the number of lines, words and characters in the file only.
# Here, we use the command below to give us the number of lines only.
# We can use the -l flag for lines.
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ grep NNNNNN NGS0001.R1.fastq | wc -l
555

# Here, we changed the directory to data directory and we used the cut command to extract columns from files.
# '-f1,2,3' means to cut these columns from the dataset.
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data/untrimmed_fastq$ cd ~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$ cut -f1,2,3 annotation.bed | head -n 5
chr1    14362   14829
chr1    14969   15038
chr1    15795   15947
chr1    16606   16765
chr1    16857   17055

# Cut these columns from the whole dataset and not just the first 5 lines
# We saved it as a file
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$ cut -f1,2,3 annotation.bed > annotation.bed_cut

# Extracting genomic coordinates of exon features:
# We only want the RABL2B exons, so we have to use grep to only keep the exon lines and save to RABL2B_exons file
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$ grep RABL2B annotation.bed > RABL2B_exons

# The command below counts the number of lines in the file
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$ cat annotation.bed | wc -l
201071

# ls command is used to list what inside this directory
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$ ls
annotation.bed    annotation.bed_cut    hg19.fa.gz    other         trimmed_fastq
annotation.bed.1  annotation_plus5.bed  hg19.fa.gz.1  RABL2B_exons  untrimmed_fastq

# To make a copy of the file, we used the command below:
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$ cp annotation.bed annotation_plus5.bed
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$ ls
annotation.bed    annotation.bed_cut    hg19.fa.gz    other         trimmed_fastq
annotation.bed.1  annotation_plus5.bed  hg19.fa.gz.1  RABL2B_exons  untrimmed_fastq

# This command adds (appends) the first 5 lines of the file to itself
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$ head -5 annotation.bed >> annotation_plus5.bed/

# the command below shows us the number of lines should be +5 now
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$ cat annotation_plus5.bed | wc -l
201076

# We can use sort command to remove exons.
# Sort command with the -u option to return only unique lines.
# The command below shows us the line count should be the original one now
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$ sort -u annotation_plus5.bed | wc -l
201071
(base) ubuntu@mai:~/ngs_course/dnaseq/data$
